Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
A Charitable Interpretation of Mu'tazila and Khawarij
Author's charitable interpretation of Mu'tazila and Khawarij and reinterpretation of Nasafi's takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's charitable reinterpretation of Nasafi's takfir as kufr al-ni'ma rather than kufr al-milla, and his defence of the intentions of Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Takfir can mean ingratitude, not apostasy—a crucial distinction.

After disagreeing with Nasafi's takfir, the author goes further to offer a positive reinterpretation of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. He explains their motivations and finally suggests that Nasafi's declaration might refer to a lesser form of disbelief. Let's explore this important nuance.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's defence of Mu'tazila
Notice how the author praises the Mu'tazila for their role in defending Islam against external philosophies. This is a charitable view.
He doesn't endorse all their views but respects their intention.
2
Read the defence of Khawarij
The author explains that the Khawarij were strict because they saw deviation from the creed. He acknowledges their error in declaring the Companions disbelievers but calls it a slip of zeal.
He hopes for a future generation that will reconcile without takfir.
3
Understand the key reinterpretation
The author reinterprets Nasafi's takfir as kufr al-ni'ma (disbelief of blessing/ingratitude) not kufr al-milla (apostasy), supported by Quran 4:116 which says God forgives what is less than shirk.
This allows Nasafi's severity to be understood as rhetorical rather than excommunicative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنسفي يكفر الخوارج والمعتزلة لقولهم في مرتكب الكبيرة، مستدلا على ذلك بأنهم يئسوا من رحمة الله، وقد قال تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّهُ لَا يَأْيَنَسُ مِن زَوْعِ اللَّهِ إِلَّا الْقَوْمُ الكَفِرُونَ ﴾ [يوسف: ۸۷] ويدير حول كلامه هذا نقاشا عقليا ليؤكد رأيه في كفر المعتزلة والخوارج. وأخالف الإمام النسفي في رأيه في هذا فإنه على رأي أهل السنة - والنسفي منهم - إن الإيمان هو التصديق وهو موجود لدى المعتزلة والخوارج، حتى لو اختلفنا في تعريف الإيمان، ورائي في ذلك أن المعتزلة كان جل همهم الدفاع عن الإسلام ورد الضربات والشطحات العقلية الموجهة إليه من الفلسفات الأخرى بل والديانات الأخرى. ولقد كان هدف الخوارج من تكفير مرتكب الكبيرة هو أن يلتزم المسلمون بكل ما جاء به القرآن والسنة المطهرة، فهم فقط شددوا لأنهم رأوا الخروج عن العقيدة. وهم زلوا حينما كفروا الصحابة الأعلام - رضوان الله عليهم - لكني أحتسبها لهم سقطة عصبية، وأحسب أن جيلا طاهرا من المسلمين يأتي لينقي المجرى الطاهر من كل الشوائب التي علقت به معطيا كل اتجاه إسلامي حقه دون تكفير. وقول الله سبحانه وتعالى خير شاهد على ما أراه: إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذَلِكَ لِمَن يَشَاءُ [النساء: ١١٦] ويمكنني حمل تكفير النسفي للمعتزلة والخوارج في أنه لا يريد كفر الملة أو المعتقد وإنما كفر النعمة الذي هو كفر العصيان.
And al-Nasafi declares the Khawarij and the Mu'tazila as disbelievers due to their statement about the committer of a major sin, adducing that they have despaired of the mercy of Allah, and He said: 'Indeed, none despairs of the relief of Allah except the disbelieving people' [Yusuf 87]. And he conducts a rational discussion around this statement to affirm his view on the disbelief of the Mu'tazila and the Khawarij. And I disagree with Imam al-Nasafi in his opinion on this; for according to the view of Ahl al-Sunna—and al-Nasafi is among them—indeed faith is affirmation (tasdiq), and it is present among the Mu'tazila and the Khawarij, even if we differ in the definition of faith. My view in this is that the Mu'tazila's main concern was defending Islam and repelling the intellectual blows and excesses directed against it from other philosophies and even other religions. And the goal of the Khawarij in declaring the committer of a major sin a disbeliever was that Muslims should adhere to everything brought by the Qur'an and the purified Sunna; they only became strict because they saw deviation from the creed. And they slipped when they declared the prominent Companions—may Allah be pleased with them—disbelievers, but I consider that for them a mistake of zeal. And I think that a pure generation of Muslims will come to purify the pure course from all the impurities that have clung to it, giving every Islamic direction its due without declaring disbelief. And the saying of Allah Almighty is the best witness to my view: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive associating partners with Him, and He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [al-Nisa' 116]. And I can interpret al-Nasafi's declaration of disbelief of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij as meaning that he does not intend disbelief in the religion or creed (kufr al-milla), but rather disbelief of the blessing (kufr al-ni'ma), which is the disbelief of disobedience.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage first presents al-Nasafi's strong stance: he declares the Mu'tazila and Khawarij disbelievers because of their view on the major sinner, citing Quran 12:87 that only disbelievers despair of God's mercy. The author then disagrees with al-Nasafi. He argues that both Mu'tazila and Khawarij possess tasdiq (affirmation), which is the essence of faith according to Ahl al-Sunna, so they cannot be real disbelievers. He offers a charitable interpretation: the Mu'tazila were defending Islam against external philosophies, and the Khawarij were zealous in enforcing Islamic law, though they erred in declaring the Companions disbelievers. He suggests that a future pure generation will reconcile these schools without takfir. Finally, he interprets al-Nasafi's takfir as kufr al-ni'ma (disbelief of blessing, i.e., ingratitude) rather than kufr al-milla (disbelief in the religion), citing Quran 4:116 to show that sins less than shirk may be forgiven. This lesson presents a major objection to Nasafi's position and a conciliatory conclusion.

Key Terms
كفر الملة
كفر النعمة
كفر العصيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that any accusation of disbelief from a scholar means the person is outright apostate.
Correction: The author shows that 'kufr' can be used in different senses; kufr al-ni'ma is not the same as leaving Islam.

Checkpoint
What does the author suggest Nasafi meant by 'kufr' when referring to the Mu'tazila and Khawarij?
A) Kufr al-milla (religious disbelief)
B) Kufr al-ni'ma (ingratitude)
C) Kufr al-jahl (ignorance)
D) Kufr al-inad (obstinate rejection)

Key Takeaway
Takfir of entire groups should be interpreted charitably, as kufr al-ni'ma rather than absolute apostasy, preserving the unity of Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difference in religious opinion, do you immediately assume the other is wrong, or do you, like the author, seek a charitable interpretation? Will you commit to applying husn al-zann to Muslims you disagree with, even those you consider extreme?
?
The author describes the Khawarij's error as a 'mistake of zeal.' Have you ever been so zealous in your faith that you unfairly judged another Muslim? How would acknowledging kufr al-ni'ma change your response to someone committing a major sin?
?
The author prays for a future generation to purify the 'pure course.' What impurities of takfir and division might you be perpetuating? Will you take a concrete step today to give 'every Islamic direction its due without declaring disbelief'?

Intercession for Major Sinners and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Al-Nasafi establishes intercession for major sinners and refutes Mu'tazila with hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunna position on intercession for major sinners and how al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazila and Kharijite objections using hadith.

Core Idea
Intercession is for major sinners, affirmed by explicit prophetic hadith.

This lesson presents al-Nasafi’s argument for the reality of intercession (shafa‘a) for those who commit major sins, a hallmark of Sunni creed. He first establishes the logical basis—since Allah can forgive major sins, He can accept intercession—then refutes the Mu‘tazila who deny it, citing the Prophet’s own words. The passage is a concise proof-and-refutation that anchors Sunni hope in divine mercy while addressing scriptural objections.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Sunni premise
Read the opening statement: if Allah can forgive major sins, then He can accept intercession from prophets and others. This is the logical foundation.
Note that this flows from the Sunni view that major sins do not remove one from faith.
2
Examine the Mu'tazila objection
Al-Nasafi presents the Mu'tazila arguments: a major sinner is a wrongdoer, and the Qur'an says wrongdoers have no intercessor; also, intercession would encourage sin.
They rely on verse 40:18 and their own theological principles.
3
Analyze the first hadith refutation
The Prophet explicitly said, 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my community.' This directly counters the Mu'tazila position.
The hadith is authenticated by Ibn Majah and al-Hakim.
4
Understand the response to proof-texts
Al-Nasafi explains that hadiths the Mu'tazila and Kharijites use apply to those who consider sin permissible, not to repentant sinners.
5
Reflect on the second hadith
The Prophet said, 'Whoever says there is no god but God will enter Paradise, even if he commits adultery or steals.' This shows that faith alone secures ultimate salvation despite major sins.
This hadith is from Muslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في إثبات الشفاعة.
لما جاز أن يغفر الله لمرتكب الكبيرة على رأي أهل السنة، جاز له سبحانه أن يقبل الشفاعة من الرسل الأطهار والآباء وغيرهم.
ويذكر النسفي رأي المعتزلة بامتناعها، وذلك بناء على رأيهم في صاحب الكبيرة ويقدم أدلتهم منها قوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] فمرتكب الكبيرة ظالم، والله تعالى لا يحب من أبغضه، والشفاعة تكون للمطيع لا للعاصي - كما أن الشفاعة لأهل الكبائر تجرئة للناس على الذنوب.
ثم يبدأ في مناقشتهم ليبطل أقوالهم، مستدلا بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر في أمتي" والحديث صحيح رواه ابن ماجه في سننه من حديث جابر ج ١٤٤١ ورواه الحاكم في المستدرك من حديث أنس بن مالك ج ١ ص ٦٩.
ويقول: إن ما استدل به المعتزلة والخوارج من الأحاديث إنما يحمل على المستحل ويدعم كلامه بما روي عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: "من قال لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنة وإن زنى وإن سرق" والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم من حديث أبي ذر ج ٢ ص ٩٤.
The discourse on establishing intercession.
When it is permissible for God to forgive the committer of a major sin according to the view of Ahl al-Sunna, it is permissible for Him, exalted, to accept intercession from the pure messengers, the fathers, and others.
And al-Nasafi mentions the view of the Mu'tazila that it is impossible, and that is based on their view regarding the committer of a major sin. He presents their evidence, including His statement, exalted: 'For the wrongdoers there is no protector and no intercessor to be obeyed' [Ghafir: 18]. So the committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer, and God, exalted, does not love one He hates, and intercession is for the obedient, not the disobedient — and also that intercession for people of major sins is an encouragement for people to commit sins.
Then he begins to refute them to invalidate their statements, adducing the statement of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my community' — and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Ibn Majah in his Sunan from the hadith of Jabir (vol. 1441) and narrated by al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak from the hadith of Anas ibn Malik (vol. 1, p. 69).
And he says: What the Mu'tazila and Kharijites adduce from the hadith is only to be interpreted as referring to the one who considers [sin] permissible. And he supports his statement with what is narrated from the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, that he said: 'Whoever says there is no god but God will enter Paradise, even if he commits adultery and even if he steals' — and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Muslim from the hadith of Abu Dharr (vol. 2, p. 94).
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This is a proof-and-refutation passage. Al-Nasafi first states the Ahl al-Sunna position that since God can forgive major sins, He can also accept intercession from prophets, righteous ancestors, and others. He then presents the Mu'tazila objection: they deny intercession for major sinners based on their view of the grave sinner (the committer of a major sin is a wrongdoer, and God does not love him; intercession is only for the obedient, not the disobedient). They also argue that intercession encourages sin. Al-Nasafi then refutes them by citing a hadith where the Prophet explicitly says, 'My intercession is for the people of major sins among my community.' He also explains that the hadiths used by the Mu'tazila and Kharijites apply to those who consider sin permissible, not to repentant sinners. He further supports this with another authentic hadith: 'Whoever says there is no god but God will enter Paradise, even if he commits adultery or steals,' showing that faith alone suffices for ultimate salvation despite major sins.

Key Terms
شفاعة
كبيرة
معتزلة
خوارج
جرأة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession is only for minor sins or for obedient believers, not for major sinners.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly said his intercession is for the people of major sins in his community, and faith alone leads to Paradise despite sins.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main argument of the Mu'tazila against intercession for major sinners?
A) Major sinners are hypocrites and cannot be forgiven.
B) Intercession is only for the obedient, not the disobedient.
C) Major sins are unforgivable.
D) Intercession was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Intercession for major sinners is proven by the Qur’anic principle of forgiveness and authenticated hadith, contrary to Mu‘tazila claims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's mercy through intercession can cover your worst sins, or do you secretly think some sins are too great? What would it mean for you to live with that hope today?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you feel the weight of that statement as a commitment to turn away from sin, or do you treat it as a magic formula that leaves your heart unchanged?
?
If the Prophet's intercession is for people of major sins, what sin are you holding onto that you need to confess and repent from right now — not tomorrow, but today? What is stopping you?

The Necessity of Appointing an Imam
Nasafi argues necessity of imamate and refutes a counterargument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that appointing an imam is necessary even in the most virtuous society, using the Companions' consensus as evidence.

Core Idea
Even the best community needed an imam; the Companions proved it.

This passage introduces the foundational argument for the necessity of imamate in Islamic political thought. Imam Nasafi counters the objection that a just society could dispense with a leader by pointing to the historical example of the righteous Companions, who immediately appointed a successor after the Prophet's death.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
This is an editorial summary of Nasafi's original text.
2
Identify Nasafi's core claim and the objection
Find where Nasafi states the necessity of an imam and the role of the imam. Then locate the counterargument: some say if people refrained from injustice, they would not need an imam.
3
Analyze the historical evidence
Notice how Nasafi uses the Companions' example to refute the objection. Ask yourself: Why does he consider their era the most virtuous? What does their action prove?
The Companions appointed Abu Bakr despite living in an era of high moral standards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الإمامة: يبدأ في موضوع الإمامة ببيان أهميتها، وضرورة تنصيب الإمام، لأنه هو الذي يقوم بشئون البلاد في السلم والحرب، ويحافظ على استقلالها السياسي، والاقتصادي والاجتماعي. ويقول : إنه لا عبرة بقول من يقول : - إن الناس لو كفوا عن المظالم لأغناهم الأمر عن تنصيب إمام - ويستشهد في رده لهذا القول أن عصر الصحابة كان من أنزه العصور، ومع ذلك أسرعوا إلى تنصيب أبي بكر، فعمر، فعثمان، فعلی،
Discussion on imamate: He begins the topic of imamate by explaining its importance and the necessity of appointing an imam, because he is the one who manages the affairs of the country in peace and war, and preserves its political, economic, and social independence. And he says: There is no regard for the saying of those who say: 'If people refrained from injustices, they would be made independent of appointing an imam.' And he cites in refutation of this saying that the era of the Companions was the most virtuous of eras, yet they hastened to appoint Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then 'Uthman, then 'Ali.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is an editorial summary of Nasafi's discussion on imamate. It opens by stating that imamate is important and the appointment of an imam is necessary because the imam manages state affairs in peace and war and maintains political, economic, and social independence. Nasafi then refutes the objection that if people abstained from injustice, they would have no need for an imam. He points to the example of the Companions: despite living in the most virtuous era, they promptly appointed Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then 'Uthman, then 'Ali as successive leaders. This historical fact demonstrates that even the best community needed a leader to prevent conflict and ensure order, invalidating the hypothetical argument against imamate. The passage is truncated, but the core argument is clear.

Key Terms
الإمامة
تنصيب الإمام
الصحابة
أبو بكر
عمر
عثمان
علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A perfectly just society does not need a leader.
Correction: Nasafi argues that even the most virtuous society, the Companions, needed an imam, as shown by their immediate appointment of Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
What historical example does Nasafi use to prove the necessity of an imam?
A) The Prophet's own leadership in Medina.
B) The haste of the Companions to appoint Abu Bakr after the Prophet's death.
C) The unjust rulers of the Umayyads.
D) The saying of 'Ali that there must always be a leader.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi proves the necessity of imamate by showing that even the most righteous community, the Companions, immediately appointed a leader.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever resist following a leader or scholar because you think you can manage your own affairs without guidance? How does the Companions' example challenge that attitude?
?
If the most virtuous generation needed an imam, what does that say about your own need for communal religious leadership? Will you commit to supporting a legitimate leader or scholar in your community?
?
When you see disputes among Muslims, do you tend to withdraw rather than unite behind a leader? How can you practically follow the Companions' hastening to appoint a leader even in times of unity?

The Obligation of Appointing an Imam
Al-Nasafi argues for the obligation of appointing an imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why appointing an imam is obligatory, based on the example of the Companions and the Prophet's warning about dying without a leader.

Core Idea
The imam is not optional; even the best generations immediately appointed one.

Al-Nasafi opens his discussion on the imamate by establishing its fundamental importance. He argues that the appointment of an imam is not a matter of convenience but a religious obligation, refuting those who think it can be dispensed with if people are just. The evidence from the early community and a prophetic hadith sets the tone for the entire doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on necessity
Read the Arabic passage that explains why an imam is needed and the refutation of the objection.
Notice the argument from the Companions' actions.
2
Identify the prophetic evidence
Find the hadith used to support the obligation. Reflect on its wording: 'Whoever dies without a general imam dies a death of ignorance.'
This hadith is a cornerstone for Sunni political theology.
3
Understand the refutation
Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that if people avoid injustice, an imam is unnecessary. What is the flaw in that argument according to the passage?
The example of the righteous Companions shows that even they needed an imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الإمامة: يبدأ في موضوع الإمامة ببيان أهميتها، وضرورة تنصيب الإمام، لأنه هو الذي يقوم بشئون البلاد في السلم والحرب، ويحافظ على استقلالها السياسي، والاقتصادي والاجتماعي. ويقول : إنه لا عبرة بقول من يقول : - إن الناس لو كفوا عن المظالم لأغناهم الأمر عن تنصيب إمام - ويستشهد في رده لهذا القول أن عصر الصحابة كان من أنزه العصور، ومع ذلك أسرعوا إلى تنصيب أبي بكر، فعمر، فعثمان، فعلی، ويؤكد المعنى السابق بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "مَنْ مات وليس له إمام عامة فقد مات ميتة جاهلية" ، وعلى هذا فإن تنصيب الإمام واجب. أنه لابد من ظهور الإمام، وحضوره حتى يحصل المقصود منه، ويبين بذلك يبطل قول الروافض القائلين بإمام غائب. ولا يجوز تنصيبه أكثر من إمام في وقت واحد، لما فيه من تفريق كلمة الأمة، وإيجاد سبب للتنازع والتطاحن إلا إذا وجد حاجز كبير يمنع من نصرة البعض البعض الآخر . وإذا عقدت الإمامة لاثنين في وقت واحد اختير أحدهما، أو يعقد لغيرهما ممن يصلح للإمامة، وهو بذلك يبطل قول الروافض الذين يثبتون إماما ناطقا وإماما صامتا، وقول الكرامية القائلين بصحة إمامة على، ومعاوية في وقت واحد. وعدد النسفي شروط من يصلح للإمامة، ومنها: أ- أن الإمامة لا تكون إلا فى قبيلة قريش، خلافا لقول الروافض بأنها لا تصلح إلا من بني هاشم، وخلافا لقول الراوندية القائلين بالوراثة. ويؤيد رأيه هذا بقول الرسول عليه السلام: "الأئمة من قريش"، والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم جـ ۱۲ ص ۲۰۲ من حديث جابر بن سمرة عن النبي . وبقصة ثقيفة بني ساعدة. ب- يذكر النسفي الأوصاف التي لو توفرت في واحد صار أهلا للإمامة ومنها: أن يكون بلغ مبلغ المجتهدين في الفقه، وأن يكون عدلا ورعا، وأن يكون مهتديا إلى وجه السياسات والتدابير عارفا بمراتب الناس، في قمة الذكاء، جامعا بين الصرامة واللين، وأن يكون شجاعا. ثم يقول: إن وجودها كلها فيه ليس بشرط، والدليل على ذلك أن الخلافة انعقدت بعد الخلفاء الراشدين لمن لم يبلغوا في العلم مبلغ الاجتهاد.
Discussion on the Imamate: He begins the topic of the Imamate by explaining its importance and the necessity of appointing an imam, because it is he who manages the affairs of the country in peace and war, and preserves its political, economic, and social independence. He says: No heed is given to the saying of one who says 'If people refrained from injustices, they would be spared the need to appoint an imam.' In refutation of this saying, he cites that the era of the Companions was among the most virtuous of eras, yet they hastened to appoint Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. He affirms the previous meaning by the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever dies without having a general imam dies a death of ignorance.' Thus, the appointment of an imam is obligatory. He explains that the imam must appear and be present so that the intended purpose is achieved, and by this he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who claim a hidden imam. It is not permissible to appoint more than one imam at one time, because that would cause division of the community's word and create a cause for dispute and conflict, unless there is a great barrier preventing some from supporting others. If the imamate is contracted for two at one time, one of them is chosen, or it is contracted for another person who is suitable for the imamate. Thus, he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who affirm a speaking imam and a silent imam, and the saying of the Karramiyya who deem valid the imamate of Ali and Muawiya at the same time. And al-Nasafi enumerated the conditions for one who is suitable for the imamate, among them: a) The imamate is only in the tribe of Quraysh, contrary to the saying of the Rawafid that it is only from Banu Hashim, and contrary to the saying of the Rawandiyya who claim inheritance. He supports this view with the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The imams are from Quraysh,' and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Muslim vol. 12 p. 202 from Jabir ibn Samura from the Prophet, and with the story of the Saqifa of Banu Sa'ida. b) Al-Nasafi mentions the qualities that if present in one person make him worthy of the imamate, including: that he has reached the level of the mujtahids in fiqh, that he is just and pious, that he is guided to the way of policies and measures, knowledgeable of the ranks of people, of the highest intelligence, combining severity and gentleness, and that he is courageous. Then he says: The presence of all of them in him is not a condition, and evidence for this is that the caliphate was contracted after the Rightly Guided Caliphs for those who had not reached the level of ijtihad in knowledge.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a modern summary of al-Nasafi's discussion on the imamate. It begins by stating the importance of the imam as the manager of state affairs and preserver of independence. Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that an imam is unnecessary if people refrain from injustice, using the example of the righteous Companions who immediately appointed successors. He cites the hadith that one who dies without a general imam dies a death of ignorance, establishing the obligation of appointment. He then argues that the imam must be present (not hidden), thereby refuting the Rafidah belief in a hidden imam. He asserts that only one imam is allowed at a time, unless geographic barriers prevent unity, and if two are contracted, one must be chosen; this refutes both the Rafidah notion of a speaking and silent imam and the Karramiyya allowance of concurrent imams of Ali and Muawiya. Al-Nasafi then lists conditions: the imam must be from Quraysh (supporting with hadith and the Saqifa story), and he must have qualifications such as ijtihad level in fiqh, justice, political acumen, intelligence, balance, and courage. However, he clarifies that possessing all these qualities is not a condition, as after the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the caliphate was given to those who were not mujtahids. This shows a pragmatic approach to the imamate.

Key Terms
الإمامة
تنصيب الإمام
إمام عامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if people are just and avoid injustice, an imam is unnecessary.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that even the just Companions needed an imam; the imam is not only for preventing injustice but for managing the community.

Checkpoint
What evidence does al-Nasafi use to refute the claim that an imam is unnecessary if people avoid injustice?
A) The intellectual consensus of scholars.
B) The example of the Companions who immediately appointed imams.
C) The fact that the Prophet himself did not appoint a successor.
D) The Quranic verses on obedience.

Key Takeaway
Appointing an imam is obligatory, as proven by the practice of the Companions and a prophetic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you prioritize personal freedom over community leadership, are you repeating the error of those who say 'if people refrained from injustices, no imam would be needed'? What would the Companions think of your attitude?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) warned that dying without a general imam is a death of ignorance. Do you live as if this warning applies to you? What concrete action will you take to ensure you are not among those who die in ignorance?
?
You may think the imamate is irrelevant to your daily life. But Al-Nasafi points out that even the most righteous generation appointed imams immediately. How does your indifference compare to their urgency? What will you change today?

The Imam Must Be Present and Only One at a Time
Al-Nasafi refutes hidden and multiple imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imam must be present and why having two imams is impermissible, refuting sectarian views.

Core Idea
One present imam preserves unity; hidden or multiple imams cause division.

After establishing the obligation of an imam, al-Nasafi addresses two crucial issues: the imam must be physically present (not hidden) and there can only be one at a time. These points directly refute the beliefs of the Rawafid (who believe in a hidden imam and a speaking/silent imam) and the Karramiyya (who allowed concurrent imams).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on presence and unity
Read the Arabic text that discusses the necessity of the imam's appearance and the prohibition of multiple imams.
Note the conditional exception for a great barrier.
2
Identify the refuted sects
Find where al-Nasafi explicitly names the Rawafid and Karramiyya and their specific claims.
Rawafid: hidden imam + speaking/silent imam. Karramiyya: concurrent imams of Ali and Muawiya.
3
Understand the rationale
Why is it impermissible to have two imams? The passage mentions division of the community and conflict.
Also note the exception: if there is a great barrier preventing support.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الإمامة: يبدأ في موضوع الإمامة ببيان أهميتها، وضرورة تنصيب الإمام، لأنه هو الذي يقوم بشئون البلاد في السلم والحرب، ويحافظ على استقلالها السياسي، والاقتصادي والاجتماعي. ويقول : إنه لا عبرة بقول من يقول : - إن الناس لو كفوا عن المظالم لأغناهم الأمر عن تنصيب إمام - ويستشهد في رده لهذا القول أن عصر الصحابة كان من أنزه العصور، ومع ذلك أسرعوا إلى تنصيب أبي بكر، فعمر، فعثمان، فعلی، ويؤكد المعنى السابق بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "مَنْ مات وليس له إمام عامة فقد مات ميتة جاهلية" ، وعلى هذا فإن تنصيب الإمام واجب. أنه لابد من ظهور الإمام، وحضوره حتى يحصل المقصود منه، ويبين بذلك يبطل قول الروافض القائلين بإمام غائب. ولا يجوز تنصيبه أكثر من إمام في وقت واحد، لما فيه من تفريق كلمة الأمة، وإيجاد سبب للتنازع والتطاحن إلا إذا وجد حاجز كبير يمنع من نصرة البعض البعض الآخر . وإذا عقدت الإمامة لاثنين في وقت واحد اختير أحدهما، أو يعقد لغيرهما ممن يصلح للإمامة، وهو بذلك يبطل قول الروافض الذين يثبتون إماما ناطقا وإماما صامتا، وقول الكرامية القائلين بصحة إمامة على، ومعاوية في وقت واحد. وعدد النسفي شروط من يصلح للإمامة، ومنها: أ- أن الإمامة لا تكون إلا فى قبيلة قريش، خلافا لقول الروافض بأنها لا تصلح إلا من بني هاشم، وخلافا لقول الراوندية القائلين بالوراثة. ويؤيد رأيه هذا بقول الرسول عليه السلام: "الأئمة من قريش"، والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم جـ ۱۲ ص ۲۰۲ من حديث جابر بن سمرة عن النبي . وبقصة ثقيفة بني ساعدة. ب- يذكر النسفي الأوصاف التي لو توفرت في واحد صار أهلا للإمامة ومنها: أن يكون بلغ مبلغ المجتهدين في الفقه، وأن يكون عدلا ورعا، وأن يكون مهتديا إلى وجه السياسات والتدابير عارفا بمراتب الناس، في قمة الذكاء، جامعا بين الصرامة واللين، وأن يكون شجاعا. ثم يقول: إن وجودها كلها فيه ليس بشرط، والدليل على ذلك أن الخلافة انعقدت بعد الخلفاء الراشدين لمن لم يبلغوا في العلم مبلغ الاجتهاد.
Discussion on the Imamate: He begins the topic of the Imamate by explaining its importance and the necessity of appointing an imam, because it is he who manages the affairs of the country in peace and war, and preserves its political, economic, and social independence. He says: No heed is given to the saying of one who says 'If people refrained from injustices, they would be spared the need to appoint an imam.' In refutation of this saying, he cites that the era of the Companions was among the most virtuous of eras, yet they hastened to appoint Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. He affirms the previous meaning by the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever dies without having a general imam dies a death of ignorance.' Thus, the appointment of an imam is obligatory. He explains that the imam must appear and be present so that the intended purpose is achieved, and by this he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who claim a hidden imam. It is not permissible to appoint more than one imam at one time, because that would cause division of the community's word and create a cause for dispute and conflict, unless there is a great barrier preventing some from supporting others. If the imamate is contracted for two at one time, one of them is chosen, or it is contracted for another person who is suitable for the imamate. Thus, he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who affirm a speaking imam and a silent imam, and the saying of the Karramiyya who deem valid the imamate of Ali and Muawiya at the same time. And al-Nasafi enumerated the conditions for one who is suitable for the imamate, among them: a) The imamate is only in the tribe of Quraysh, contrary to the saying of the Rawafid that it is only from Banu Hashim, and contrary to the saying of the Rawandiyya who claim inheritance. He supports this view with the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The imams are from Quraysh,' and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Muslim vol. 12 p. 202 from Jabir ibn Samura from the Prophet, and with the story of the Saqifa of Banu Sa'ida. b) Al-Nasafi mentions the qualities that if present in one person make him worthy of the imamate, including: that he has reached the level of the mujtahids in fiqh, that he is just and pious, that he is guided to the way of policies and measures, knowledgeable of the ranks of people, of the highest intelligence, combining severity and gentleness, and that he is courageous. Then he says: The presence of all of them in him is not a condition, and evidence for this is that the caliphate was contracted after the Rightly Guided Caliphs for those who had not reached the level of ijtihad in knowledge.
Source pages p. 116

Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that an imam is unnecessary if people refrain from injustice, using the example of the righteous Companions who immediately appointed successors. إمام ناطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe in a hidden imam or that two imams can rule simultaneously.
Correction: Al-Nasafi insists the imam must be present and only one at a time to avoid division.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if two people are contracted for the imamate at the same time?
A) Both are accepted as co-imams.
B) One is chosen, or a new suitable person is appointed.
C) The contract is void and no imam is needed.
D) A lottery is held.

Key Takeaway
The imam must be present and singular; any belief in a hidden or multiple imams is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever silently followed a ‘hidden’ authority—an idea, a leader, or a group—that prevented you from fully submitting to the present leadership of your community? How has that affected your loyalty and unity?
?
In your own life, where do you tend to create ‘multiple imams’—splitting your allegiance between competing priorities, groups, or authorities? What would it cost you to consolidate that allegiance under one single guide?
?
The exception for a ‘great barrier’ shows that unity is the norm, not division. Is there a barrier in your heart—pride, fear, or attachment—that keeps you from uniting with the community? Will you remove it today?

5 min
The Imam Must Be from Quraysh
Al-Nasafi establishes the Quraysh condition and refutes sectarian alternatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition that the imam must be from the tribe of Quraysh, and how this refutes narrow Hashimite exclusivity and inheritance claims.

Core Idea
The imam is from Quraysh, not only from Banu Hashim or by inheritance.

Al-Nasafi presents one of the most debated conditions of the imamate: the imam must be from the tribe of Quraysh. He uses a well-known hadith and the historical precedent of the Saqifa to support this. He simultaneously refutes the Rawafid (who restrict it to Banu Hashim) and the Rawandiyya (who claim it passes by inheritance).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Quraysh
Read the Arabic text that states the imamate is only from Quraysh and refutes other claims.
Notice the two refuted groups: Rawafid and Rawandiyya.
2
Examine the evidence
Al-Nasafi cites the hadith 'The imams are from Quraysh' and the story of Saqifa. Why are these evidence?
The hadith is from Muslim, authentic.
3
Differentiate the refutations
The Rawafid say only from Banu Hashim; the Rawandiyya say inheritance. How does al-Nasafi's condition refute both?
Quraysh is broader than Hashim, and not hereditary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Which two groups does al-Nasafi oppose with the Quraysh condition?
A) Shia and Khawarij.
B) Rawafid and Rawandiyya.
C) Karramiyya and Murji'ah.
D) Mu'tazila and Ash'ariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever favoured a leader from your own family or tribe, even when others were more qualified? This lesson teaches that leadership in Islam is based on belonging to the broader Quraysh, not on clan loyalty. Where in your life do you need to prioritize unity over blood ties? What will you change?
?
The Rawandiyya believed imamate is inherited. Do you sometimes assume your children will automatically inherit your faith or status? This lesson calls you to earn your place through deeds. What is one thing you will actively teach your children to prepare them to be worthy of leadership in Allah's sight, not by birthright but by character?
?
You just learned that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'The imams are from Quraysh.' Does this hadith sit uncomfortably with modern ideas of equality? If so, examine your heart: are you willing to accept Allah's decree and the Prophet's guidance even when it challenges your assumptions about merit and lineage? How will you submit to this teaching in your daily life?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
5 min
Qualifications of the Imam (And Their Flexibility)
Al-Nasafi lists imam's ideal qualities and notes they are not all mandatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the desirable qualities of an imam (such as ijtihad, justice, political acumen) and that not all are required, as shown by historical practice.

Core Idea
The imam should be qualified, but perfection is not a condition.

Al-Nasafi concludes his discussion by listing the ideal qualities an imam should possess: knowledge, justice, wisdom, intelligence, and courage. However, he immediately clarifies that the presence of all these qualities is not a condition for validity. He gives evidence from the later caliphs who were not mujtahids. This pragmatic approach balances idealism with reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on qualities
Read the Arabic text that lists the qualities and the statement that they are not all required.
Note the specific qualities mentioned.
2
Identify the key point
Al-Nasafi says 'their presence in him all is not a condition.' Why? What evidence does he give?
The evidence: later caliphs were not mujtahids.
3
Reflect on practical implications
Why might it be important that not all conditions are required?
It allows for flexibility in choosing leaders.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الإمامة: يبدأ في موضوع الإمامة ببيان أهميتها، وضرورة تنصيب الإمام، لأنه هو الذي يقوم بشئون البلاد في السلم والحرب، ويحافظ على استقلالها السياسي، والاقتصادي والاجتماعي. ويقول : إنه لا عبرة بقول من يقول : - إن الناس لو كفوا عن المظالم لأغناهم الأمر عن تنصيب إمام - ويستشهد في رده لهذا القول أن عصر الصحابة كان من أنزه العصور، ومع ذلك أسرعوا إلى تنصيب أبي بكر، فعمر، فعثمان، فعلی، ويؤكد المعنى السابق بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "مَنْ مات وليس له إمام عامة فقد مات ميتة جاهلية" ، وعلى هذا فإن تنصيب الإمام واجب. أنه لابد من ظهور الإمام، وحضوره حتى يحصل المقصود منه، ويبين بذلك يبطل قول الروافض القائلين بإمام غائب. ولا يجوز تنصيبه أكثر من إمام في وقت واحد، لما فيه من تفريق كلمة الأمة، وإيجاد سبب للتنازع والتطاحن إلا إذا وجد حاجز كبير يمنع من نصرة البعض البعض الآخر . وإذا عقدت الإمامة لاثنين في وقت واحد اختير أحدهما، أو يعقد لغيرهما ممن يصلح للإمامة، وهو بذلك يبطل قول الروافض الذين يثبتون إماما ناطقا وإماما صامتا، وقول الكرامية القائلين بصحة إمامة على، ومعاوية في وقت واحد. وعدد النسفي شروط من يصلح للإمامة، ومنها: أ- أن الإمامة لا تكون إلا فى قبيلة قريش، خلافا لقول الروافض بأنها لا تصلح إلا من بني هاشم، وخلافا لقول الراوندية القائلين بالوراثة. ويؤيد رأيه هذا بقول الرسول عليه السلام: "الأئمة من قريش"، والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم جـ ۱۲ ص ۲۰۲ من حديث جابر بن سمرة عن النبي . وبقصة ثقيفة بني ساعدة. ب- يذكر النسفي الأوصاف التي لو توفرت في واحد صار أهلا للإمامة ومنها: أن يكون بلغ مبلغ المجتهدين في الفقه، وأن يكون عدلا ورعا، وأن يكون مهتديا إلى وجه السياسات والتدابير عارفا بمراتب الناس، في قمة الذكاء، جامعا بين الصرامة واللين، وأن يكون شجاعا. ثم يقول: إن وجودها كلها فيه ليس بشرط، والدليل على ذلك أن الخلافة انعقدت بعد الخلفاء الراشدين لمن لم يبلغوا في العلم مبلغ الاجتهاد.
Discussion on the Imamate: He begins the topic of the Imamate by explaining its importance and the necessity of appointing an imam, because it is he who manages the affairs of the country in peace and war, and preserves its political, economic, and social independence. He says: No heed is given to the saying of one who says 'If people refrained from injustices, they would be spared the need to appoint an imam.' In refutation of this saying, he cites that the era of the Companions was among the most virtuous of eras, yet they hastened to appoint Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. He affirms the previous meaning by the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever dies without having a general imam dies a death of ignorance.' Thus, the appointment of an imam is obligatory. He explains that the imam must appear and be present so that the intended purpose is achieved, and by this he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who claim a hidden imam. It is not permissible to appoint more than one imam at one time, because that would cause division of the community's word and create a cause for dispute and conflict, unless there is a great barrier preventing some from supporting others. If the imamate is contracted for two at one time, one of them is chosen, or it is contracted for another person who is suitable for the imamate. Thus, he invalidates the saying of the Rawafid who affirm a speaking imam and a silent imam, and the saying of the Karramiyya who deem valid the imamate of Ali and Muawiya at the same time. And al-Nasafi enumerated the conditions for one who is suitable for the imamate, among them: a) The imamate is only in the tribe of Quraysh, contrary to the saying of the Rawafid that it is only from Banu Hashim, and contrary to the saying of the Rawandiyya who claim inheritance. He supports this view with the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The imams are from Quraysh,' and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Muslim vol. 12 p. 202 from Jabir ibn Samura from the Prophet, and with the story of the Saqifa of Banu Sa'ida. b) Al-Nasafi mentions the qualities that if present in one person make him worthy of the imamate, including: that he has reached the level of the mujtahids in fiqh, that he is just and pious, that he is guided to the way of policies and measures, knowledgeable of the ranks of people, of the highest intelligence, combining severity and gentleness, and that he is courageous. Then he says: The presence of all of them in him is not a condition, and evidence for this is that the caliphate was contracted after the Rightly Guided Caliphs for those who had not reached the level of ijtihad in knowledge.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a modern summary of al-Nasafi's discussion on the imamate. It begins by stating the importance of the imam as the manager of state affairs and preserver of independence. Al-Nasafi refutes the claim that an imam is unnecessary if people refrain from injustice, using the example of the righteous Companions who immediately appointed successors. He cites the hadith that one who dies without a general imam dies a death of ignorance, establishing the obligation of appointment. He then argues that the imam must be present (not hidden), thereby refuting the Rafidah belief in a hidden imam. He asserts that only one imam is allowed at a time, unless geographic barriers prevent unity, and if two are contracted, one must be chosen; this refutes both the Rafidah notion of a speaking and silent imam and the Karramiyya allowance of concurrent imams of Ali and Muawiya. Al-Nasafi then lists conditions: the imam must be from Quraysh (supporting with hadith and the Saqifa story), and he must have qualifications such as ijtihad level in fiqh, justice, political acumen, intelligence, balance, and courage. However, he clarifies that possessing all these qualities is not a condition, as after the Rightly Guided Caliphs, the caliphate was given to those who were not mujtahids. This shows a pragmatic approach to the imamate.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد
عدالة
السياسات
شجاعة
شروط الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think an imam must be a mujtahid in all respects.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that later non-mujtahid caliphs were accepted.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Nasafi say the presence of all listed qualities is not a condition?
A) Because the Prophet did not mention them.
B) Because later caliphs after the Rashidun lacked ijtihad.
C) Because the Quran does not require them.
D) Because the Rawafid reject them.

Key Takeaway
The imam should ideally possess many qualities, but lacking some does not invalidate the imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of those who lead your community, do you find yourself demanding perfection from them, knowing that even the caliphate after the Rashidun accepted less? How has this lesson changed your view of your own responsibility to support imperfect leaders?
?
Are you personally qualified to lead? Even if not, does that mean you are excused from striving to embody the qualities Al-Nasafi listed? What are you actively doing to cultivate at least one of them?
?
Reflect: The imamate can be valid without all qualities. But does that comfort you, or challenge you to step up and fill gaps? What one quality from the list will you focus on developing starting this week?

Obligation of the Imam and Refutation of Hidden Imam
Nasafi proves the obligation of appointing an Imam and rejects the Rafidi belief in a hidden Imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the appointment of a visible Imam is obligatory upon the Muslim community, based on the Prophet's hadith, and that the belief in a hidden Imam is invalid.

Core Idea
Having a visible Imam is obligatory; a hidden Imam cannot fulfill its purpose.

This lesson focuses on a key proof from Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla. He cites a well-known hadith to establish the obligation of appointing an Imam, and then argues that the Imam must be present and active, thereby refuting the Shi'a doctrine of a hidden Imam. The passage is both constructive (proving a positive duty) and polemical (rejecting a rival view).

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith carefully
Read the Arabic hadith and its translation. Notice that it connects the absence of an Imam to a death of Jahiliyya.
The hadith is a strong warning.
2
Identify the derivation of obligation
Nasafi says 'upon this, appointment is obligatory.' Ask why the hadith implies obligation.
It's a logical inference from the severe warning.
3
Understand the condition of presence
Nasafi states that the Imam must appear and be present to achieve the purpose. Consider what purpose that might be.
Without presence, leadership functions cannot be carried out.
4
See how this refutes the hidden Imam
If the Imam must be present, then a hidden Imam cannot fulfill the requirement. This directly refutes the Rafidi belief.
The refutation is based on the purpose of Imamate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤكد المعنى السابق بقول الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: "مَنْ مات وليس له إمام عامة فقد مات ميتة جاهلية" ، وعلى هذا فإن تنصيب الإمام واجب. أنه لابد من ظهور الإمام، وحضوره حتى يحصل المقصود منه، وهو ويبين بذلك يبطل قول الروافض القائلين بإمام غائب.
And he confirms the previous meaning by the saying of the Messenger, peace be upon him: 'Whoever dies and has no Imam of the general public dies a death of Jahiliyya.' And upon this, the appointment of the Imam is obligatory. That it is necessary for the Imam to appear and be present so that the intended purpose from him is achieved, and he thereby clarifies that it invalidates the saying of the Rafidah who claim a hidden Imam.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of the Imam and a refutation of the Rafidi doctrine of a hidden Imam. Nasafi first cites the hadith of the Prophet, 'Whoever dies and has no Imam of the general public dies a death of Jahiliyya' — indicating that having an Imam is essential for Islam and its absence is akin to the pre-Islamic period of ignorance. From this hadith, he derives that the appointment (tanṣīb) of an Imam is obligatory (wājib). He then argues that the Imam must appear (ẓuhūr) and be present (ḥuḍūr) so that the intended purpose (al-maqṣūd) from him is achieved. This directly invalidates the claim of the Rafidah (Shi'a) who believe in an Imam who is hidden (ghā'ib) and not present. The logic is that a hidden Imam cannot fulfill the purpose of leadership, which requires visibility and active governance.

Key Terms
إمام عامة
موت جاهلية
تنصيب الإمام
إمام غائب
الروافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith only applies to the political Imam and does not establish a general obligation.
Correction: Nasafi uses the hadith to prove that having an Imam is obligatory for the entire community, making it a general obligation.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith 'Whoever dies without an Imam of the general public dies a death of Jahiliyya' imply according to Nasafi?
A) The Imam must be a Qurayshi.
B) The appointment of an Imam is obligatory.
C) The Imam must be infallible.
D) The Imam can be hidden.

Key Takeaway
The Imam must be visible and present; belief in a hidden Imam contradicts the purpose of Imamate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die today, would you die under the authority of a recognized Imam of the Muslim community? What concrete steps are you taking to ensure you are not in a state of spiritual ignorance like that of Jahiliyya?
?
The Prophet ﷺ warned that dying without an Imam is a death of ignorance. Does your heart feel any urgency to seek or uphold the leadership of a visible Islamic authority, or have you settled for a privatized Islam that avoids this obligation?
?
Are you willing to submit to a legitimate Imam and its rulings, even if it inconveniences your personal life? Or do you prefer a hidden, theoretical imam that doesn't challenge your comfort?

The Prohibition of Multiple Imams
Nasafi rules on the impermissibility of multiple Imams and refutes sectarian views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni scholars prohibit multiple Imams simultaneously and how this refutes certain sectarian views.

Core Idea
Multiple Imams lead to division, not unity.

Imam Nasafi presents a clear ruling: only one Imam at a time is permissible. He grounds this in the necessity of maintaining unity and preventing conflict, also addressing exceptions. This passage directly challenges the positions of the Rafidah and Karamiyya, showing the mainstream Sunni stance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the core ruling and its rationale.
Pay attention to the exception clause.
2
Identify the three cases
Notice how Nasafi presents: 1) absolute prohibition, 2) exception of a great barrier, 3) procedure if two are appointed.
This structure shows the legal reasoning.
3
Examine the refutations
See how Nasafi rejects the Rafidah and Karamiyya positions using the ruling.
Understand why their views conflict with Sunni consensus.
4
Reflect on the underlying principle
Consider why unity of the ummah is prioritized over other considerations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز تنصيبه أكثر من إمام في وقت واحد، لما فيه من تفريق كلمة الأمة، وإيجاد سبب للتنازع والتطاحن إلا إذا وجد حاجز كبير يمنع من نصرة البعض البعض الآخر . وإذا عقدت الإمامة لاثنين في وقت واحد اختير أحدهما، أو يعقد لغيرهما ممن يصلح للإمامة، وهو بذلك يبطل قول الروافض الذين يثبتون إماما ناطقا وإماما صامتا، وقول الكرامية القائلين بصحة إمامة على، ومعاوية في وقت واحد.
And it is not permissible to appoint more than one Imam at the same time, because of the division of the word of the ummah it entails, and the creation of a cause for dispute and conflict, unless there is a great barrier that prevents some from supporting others. And if the Imamate is contracted for two at the same time, one of them is chosen, or it is contracted for someone else suitable for the Imamate. And by this he invalidates the saying of the Rafidah who affirm a speaking Imam and a silent Imam, and the saying of the Karamiyya who claim the validity of the Imamate of Ali and Mu'awiya at the same time.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the impermissibility of having more than one Imam simultaneously. Nasafi states that it is not allowed to appoint more than one Imam at a time, because it causes division (tafrīq) among the Muslim community and creates reasons for conflict (tanāzu') and fighting (taṭāḥun). He makes an exception: if there is a great barrier (ḥājiz kabīr) preventing some from supporting others, then it might be allowed. However, if two are appointed, one should be chosen, or a third suitable person. Through this ruling, Nasafi refutes two groups: first, the Rafidah who claim there is both a speaking Imam (nāṭiq) and a silent Imam (ṣāmit) – referring to the Imams who are present and those hidden? Actually, 'nāṭiq' and 'ṣāmit' are concepts in Shi'ism: the speaking Imam is the one who delivers the law, the silent is the hidden one. Second, the Karamiyya who consider it valid for both Ali and Mu'awiya to be Imams at the same time, which Nasafi rejects.

Key Terms
تنازع
تطاحن
إمام ناطق
إمام صامت
الكرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The exception of a great barrier permanently justifies divided leadership.
Correction: Nasafi's exception is for extraordinary circumstances (e.g., natural barriers), not a permanent arrangement. The default is one Imam.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the ruling if two Imams are appointed at the same time?
A) Both remain in power.
B) One is chosen or a third suitable person.
C) They must both resign.
D) It is allowed if they are from Quraysh.

Key Takeaway
Sunni Islam maintains that only one Imam is permissible at a time to preserve unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been torn between two Islamic leaders or scholars, feeling that both had a claim to your allegiance? How did that affect your commitment to the unity of the Muslim community? Are you willing to accept a single legitimate authority even if it means giving up a personal preference or loyalty?
?
When you observe division among Muslims today — whether in your local mosque or in the wider ummah — do you contribute to that division by following multiple conflicting voices? What concrete step can you take this week to promote unity and avoid factionalism, in light of this lesson's emphasis on the harm of multiple leaders?

The Imam Must Be from Quraysh
Nasafi stipulates the Imam must be from Quraysh, refuting exclusivity of Hashim and inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Sunni condition that the Imam must be from Quraysh is established and how it refutes the Rafidah and Rawandiyya positions.

Core Idea
Leadership must be from Quraysh, not exclusively Hashim or hereditary.

In this passage, Nasafi presents a key condition for the Imamate: the leader must be from the tribe of Quraysh. He contrasts this with two sectarian views—the Rafidah who restrict it to the Prophet's clan, and the Rawandiyya who claim it passes by inheritance. This lesson explores the textual and historical basis for the Quraysh condition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the main condition and the refuted views.
Notice the two opposing groups mentioned.
2
Identify the two refuted positions
Nasafi refutes the Rafidah (who restrict to Banu Hashim) and the Rawandiyya (who claim inheritance). Understand their claims.
These are both non-Sunni views on Imamate.
3
Examine the evidence
Look at the hadith 'The Imams are from Quraysh' and the Saqifa story. How do they support the condition?
The Saqifa event shows the companions chose a Qurayshi leader.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعدد النسفي شروط من يصلح للإمامة، ومنها: أ- أن الإمامة لا تكون إلا فى قبيلة قريش، خلافا لقول الروافض بأنها لا تصلح إلا من بني هاشم، وخلافا لقول الراوندية القائلين بالوراثة. ويؤيد رأيه هذا بقول الرسول عليه السلام: "الأئمة من قريش"، والحديث صحيح رواه مسلم جـ ۱۲ ص ۲۰۲ من حديث جابر بن سمرة عن النبي . وبقصة ثقيفة بني ساعدة.
And al-Nasafi enumerated the conditions of one who is suitable for the Imamate, and among them: a) that the Imamate is only in the tribe of Quraysh, contrary to the saying of the Rafidah that it is only suitable from the Banu Hashim, and contrary to the saying of the Rawandiyya who claim inheritance. And he supports his opinion with the saying of the Messenger, peace be upon him: 'The Imams are from Quraysh,' and the hadith is authentic, narrated by Muslim in volume 12, page 202, from the hadith of Jabir ibn Samura from the Prophet. And with the story of Thaqifa Banu Sa'ida [or Saqifa].
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage lists the condition that the Imam must be from the tribe of Quraysh. Nasafi refutes two opposing views: the Rafidah who restrict the Imamate to the Banu Hashim (the Prophet's clan), and the Rawandiyya (a sect related to the Qarmatians? Actually Rawandiyya are those who claim inheritance of Imamate) who believe it is inherited. He supports his view with two evidences: first, the hadith 'The Imams are from Quraysh' which he notes is authentic and references Muslim's collection. Second, the historical event of Saqifa Banu Sa'ida (the meeting of the Ansar after the Prophet's death) where the Quraysh were chosen, indicating the consensus of the companions.

Key Terms
قريش
بني هاشم
الراوندية
سقيفة بني ساعدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition that the Imam must be from Quraysh is based on tribal racism or favoritism.
Correction: The condition is based on the Prophet's tribe and the consensus of the companions, not on racial superiority, but on suitability and the explicit hadith.

Checkpoint
Which group does Nasafi refute by stating the Imam must be from Quraysh and not only from Banu Hashim?
A) Karamiyya
B) Rafidah
C) Rawandiyya
D) Asha'ira

Key Takeaway
The condition that the Imam must be from Quraysh is based on the hadith and the Saqifa incident, refuting both Hashimi exclusivity and hereditary succession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the leaders you respect, do you unconsciously favor those from your own tribe, family, or ethnic group? How does this lesson's emphasis on the Prophet's tribe—yet not his family—challenge your natural biases? Will you actively seek leaders based on merit and evidence rather than familiarity?
?
The Saqifa incident was a collective decision by the companions. Are you willing to trust the collective wisdom of the Muslim community over your own preferred lineage or sect? Where in your life do you resist communal decisions that conflict with your personal attachments?
?
If the Prophet himself was from Quraysh but not his immediate family was made exclusive, what does that say about your own attachments to religious figures or dynasties? Are you holding on to any 'hereditary' or 'clan-based' notion of religious authority that this passage calls you to abandon? What would it cost you to let that go?

Imamate of the Less Excellent: Maturidi vs Ash'ari
Nasafi agrees with Maturidi that a less excellent Imam is permissible, contra Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position on the Imamate of the less excellent in the presence of a more excellent candidate, and how it differs from the Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
A less excellent Imam is valid if he has merit and righteousness.

In this passage, Nasafi aligns with the Maturidi school on a key political theology question: Can a less excellent person lead the community when a more excellent person is available? This debate between Maturidis and Ash'aris has practical implications for leadership selection. Nasafi states his position and promises to support it with evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Nasafi's claim.
2
Identify the two positions
Notice that Nasafi mentions two positions: the Maturidi view that it is permissible and the Ash'ari view that it is not.
3
Understand the conditions
Nasafi says the less excellent must possess merit (faḍl) and righteousness (ṣalāḥ) for the Imamate to be valid.
4
Consider the significance
Reflect on why this distinction matters for Islamic political thought and leadership criteria.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتحدث عن إمامة المفضول، مع وجود الأفضل، فيقول بمثل ما يقول به الماتريدي بأنها جائزة إذا توفر فيه الفضل والصلاح، وذلك خلافا لما يقوله الأشعري من أن إمامة المفضول لا تنعقد مع وجود الأفضل. ويقيم النسفي الأدلة على كلامه.
Then he discusses the Imamate of the less excellent (mafḍūl) in the presence of the more excellent (afḍal), and he says similar to what al-Maturidi says: that it is permissible if he possesses merit (faḍl) and righteousness (ṣalāḥ). This is contrary to what al-Ash'ari says, that the Imamate of the less excellent does not contract in the presence of the more excellent. And al-Nasafi establishes the evidences for his statement.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents Nasafi's position on the Imamate of the less excellent (mafḍūl) when a more excellent person (afḍal) exists. Nasafi agrees with Abu Mansur al-Maturidi that it is permissible (jā'iz) if the less excellent person has merit (faḍl) and righteousness (ṣalāḥ). This opposes the position of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who holds that the Imamate of a less excellent person does not contract (lā tan'aqid) when a more excellent one is present. Nasafi says he will provide evidences for his view, though the actual proofs are not elaborated in this passage.

Key Terms
إمامة المفضول
الأفضل
الفضل
الصلاح
الماتريدي
الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that the most excellent person must always be the Imam, and that a less excellent person's leadership is invalid.
Correction: Nasafi explains that the Imamate of the less excellent is permissible if the person possesses the necessary merit and righteousness, showing that excellence is not the sole criterion.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, when is the Imamate of the less excellent permissible in the presence of the more excellent?
A) Never
B) If he has merit and righteousness
C) Only if the more excellent refuses
D) Only if he is a Qurayshi

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi position allows a less excellent Imam provided he has merit and righteousness, unlike the stricter Ash'ari view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you choose a leader—whether in your community, workplace, or mosque—do you prioritize the most outwardly excellent or the one who truly possesses merit and righteousness? Which of these have you neglected, and what will you do to change that starting today?
?
Think of a time you dismissed a qualified person because they were not the 'best' in your eyes. How did that decision affect others? If you could revisit that moment, what would you do differently in light of Nasafi's teaching?
?
Nasafi shows that Allah allows leadership by the less excellent if they have righteousness. Are you willing to follow a righteous leader even if they are not the most talented? What fear holds you back, and how can you trust Allah's wisdom in this?

How the Imam Is Established: By Choice
Nasafi explains that the Imam is appointed by the choice of upright people, not by inheritance or nass.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Nasafi, the Imam is appointed by the choice of upright people, not by inheritance or explicit textual designation.

Core Idea
The Imam is chosen, not inherited or designated by text.

In this passage, Nasafi answers a fundamental question of political theology: who has the authority to establish the Imam? He rejects hereditary claims and secret designations, affirming that the community's righteous elite select the leader. The passage also engages with two sectarian views that must be understood to appreciate the Maturidi position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is short but dense with theological and sectarian references.
2
Identify the three positions
Nasafi presents his own view (choice of upright people) and refutes two opposing views: the Rawandiyya claim and the Jarudiyya claim. Identify each in the text.
Notice that both opposing views involve some form of inheritance or text.
3
Ask: why does the method of selection matter?
Consider why Nasafi insists on choice rather than inheritance or text. Think about how this protects the community from autocratic succession or hidden claims.
This connects to the Maturidi emphasis on communal consensus and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجيب النسفي عن السؤال التالي: بمن تثبت الإمامة؟ فيقول : تثبت باختيار أهل العدالة والصلاح، خلافا للراوندية القائلين بالوراثة، أو بنص من الرسول على العباس عمه. وخلافا للجارودية القائلين بأن النبي النص على خلافة على بالوصف، ثم ورثها ابنيه، ثم إنها على الميراث في هذين البطنين.
And al-Nasafi answers the following question: By whom is the Imamate established? He says: It is established by the choice of the people of justice and righteousness (ahl al-ʿadāla wa al-ṣalāḥ), contrary to the Rawandiyya who claim inheritance, or by a text (naṣṣ) from the Messenger regarding al-ʿAbbas his uncle. And contrary to the Jarudiyya who claim that the Prophet indicated the caliphate of Ali by description, then his two sons inherited it, then it is by inheritance in these two lines.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage addresses the question: by whom is the Imamate established (biman tathbut al-imāma)? Nasafi answers that it is established by the choice (ikhtiyār) of the people of justice and righteousness (ahl al-ʿadāla wa al-ṣalāḥ). This refutes three groups: First, the Rawandiyya who believe in inheritance (wirātha). Second, those who claim that the Messenger made a text (naṣṣ) designating al-ʿAbbas, his uncle, as successor. Third, the Jarudiyya (a Zaydi Shi'a subgroup) who claim that the Prophet indicated the caliphate of 'Ali by description (bi al-waṣf), then his two sons (Hasan and Husayn) inherited it, and then it is by inheritance in these two lineages.

Key Terms
أهل العدالة والصلاح
اختيار
الراوندية
الوراثة
نص
العباس
الجارودية
الوصف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The choice of the people of justice and righteousness is the same as a modern popular vote.
Correction: The choice is made by qualified electors (ahl al-ʿadāla wa al-ṣalāḥ), not by general public suffrage. It is a select group of upright individuals, not a democratic election.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, how is the Imam established?
A) By inheritance from the Prophet
B) By choice of the people of justice and righteousness
C) By direct designation from the Prophet
D) By the decision of the previous Imam

Key Takeaway
The Imamate is established by the choice of the people of justice and righteousness, not by inheritance or textual designation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When choosing leaders in your own life—whether in your community, workplace, or family—do you prioritize their justice and righteousness, or are you drawn to those with status, lineage, or fame? How will you change your criteria starting today?
?
The people of justice and righteousness are entrusted with the weighty task of selecting an Imam. Are you part of that group? If not, what is holding you back from becoming someone whose character and integrity qualify you to have a voice in such matters?
?
Al-Nasafi refutes those who claim that leadership belongs to a particular family by inheritance. Is there any person or position in your life that you feel entitled to because of your background or connections? Will you surrender that entitlement and submit to the principle of merit and choice, even if it costs you?

The Imamate of the Lesser: A Maturidi Perspective
Nasafi presents the Maturidi view on the permissibility of the lesser imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position on the permissibility of the imamate of the lesser individual when a better candidate exists, and how it differs from the Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
The imamate of the lesser is permissible if merit and righteousness are present.

In this lesson, we explore a key difference between Maturidi and Ash'ari thought regarding the imamate. Nasafi presents the Maturidi view that it is permissible for a less excellent person to lead if he possesses the necessary qualities, even if a more excellent person exists. This position has implications for political legitimacy in Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage about imamate of the lesser and its translation. Notice the contrasting views of al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify key terms
Focus on the terms 'إمامة المفضول' and 'الأفضل'. Understand what 'al-mafdul' and 'al-afdal' mean.
3
Compare the positions
Consider the reasoning behind each school. Why might al-Ash'ari insist on the better? Why does al-Maturidi permit the lesser?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتحدث عن إمامة المفضول، مع وجود الأفضل، فيقول بمثل ما يقول به الماتريدي بأنها جائزة إذا توفر فيه الفضل والصلاح، وذلك خلافا لما يقوله الأشعري من أن إمامة المفضول لا تنعقد مع وجود الأفضل. ويقيم النسفي الأدلة على كلامه. ثم يتكلم عن عصمة الائمة فيقول : إنها ليست بشرط، وذلك لأن العصمة مقترنة بمعجزات خارجات عن الطبائع، وهي خاصة بالأنبياء. والمكلفون بالاختيار لا يعرفون العصمة، وهذا يؤدي إلى تعطيل أمر هام، وهو الإمامة، وتكليف بما ليس في الوسع، مع أن الله تعالى يقول: لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٦].
Then he discusses the imamate of the lesser (al-mafdul) in the presence of the better (al-afdal), and he says similar to what al-Maturidi says: that it is permissible if he possesses merit and righteousness, contrary to what al-Ash'ari says – that the imamate of the lesser is not concluded in the presence of the better. And al-Nasafi adduces proofs for his statement. Then he speaks about the infallibility ('isma) of the imams and says: it is not a condition, because infallibility is tied to miracles beyond natural laws, and it is specific to prophets. And those charged with obligations by choice do not know infallibility, and this would lead to the suspension of an important matter – namely the imamate – and a burden beyond capacity, while Allah says: 'Allah does not charge a soul except [with that within] its capacity.' [Qur'an 2:286]
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage contains two related points in the context of imamate. First, Nasafi adopts the Maturidi position that the imamate of a lesser qualified person is permissible even if a more excellent person exists, opposing the Ash'ari view that it is invalid. He then moves to the topic of infallibility ('isma) of imams, arguing that it is not a condition. His reasoning is that 'isma is associated with miracles that break natural laws and is exclusive to prophets. Since the community cannot ascertain the presence of 'isma, making it a requirement would effectively paralyze the institution of imamate, imposing an impossible condition. He supports this with the Qur'anic principle that Allah does not burden anyone beyond their capacity, indicating that imamate must be accessible to ordinary human selection.

Key Terms
إمامة المفضول
ماتريدي
أشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Sunni schools agree that the best person must always be imam.
Correction: The Maturidi school permits the imamate of the lesser if he has merit and righteousness, contrary to the Ash'ari position.

Checkpoint
What is al-Maturidi's view on the imamate of the lesser in the presence of the better?
A) It is invalid.
B) It is permissible if the lesser has merit and righteousness.
C) It is always permissible regardless of merit.
D) It is only permissible if the better declines.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school permits the imamate of a lesser qualified individual if he possesses the necessary merit and righteousness, contrary to the Ash'ari position.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected the guidance or authority of someone you considered 'lesser' than another available candidate? How does this Maturidi principle challenge your attitude toward such situations?
?
When you encounter a legitimate disagreement among scholars, like the one in this passage, does it unsettle your trust in the tradition, or does it deepen your understanding? Are you willing to follow the view you believe has stronger evidence, even if it is not the majority?
?
Think of a context in your life (family, workplace, community) where a person with apparent lesser qualities is placed in authority. Do you respect their position and recognize their merit and righteousness, or do you constantly compare them to someone 'better' who is available? What would change if you truly accepted the Maturidi permission?

Infallibility: Not a Condition for Imamate
Nasafi argues against infallibility as a condition for imamate using rational and scriptural evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi rejects infallibility ('isma) as a condition for imamate and how he supports his argument with a Qur'anic verse.

Core Idea
Infallibility is exclusive to prophets and cannot be a condition for imamate.

In this lesson, we examine Nasafi's argument against making infallibility a requirement for the imam. He argues that infallibility is tied to miracles and is specific to prophets; demanding it for imams would make the imamate impossible to establish, contradicting the divine principle of not burdening beyond capacity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text about infallibility and its translation. Note how Nasafi defines 'isma and to whom it is specific.
2
Understand the logical argument
Follow Nasafi's reasoning: 'isma is unknown to the community, so requiring it would suspend the imamate and impose an impossible burden.
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic proof
Consider the cited verse (2:286) and its relevance to the argument.

?
